#SETWIDTH(128)



// we've got space issues here, to say the least
#SETWIDTH(-1)



#STARTSCRIPT(0x9E38C)

[maplabel]
// 魔導塔[buffer2char]階　
//Magic Tower Floor [buffer2char]

//Tower Floor [buffer2char]
[space2px]Tower[space3px]Floor[space3px][buffer5char][space2px]
[end]
// expanded from buffer2char to buffer4char due to a hack
// to prevent map label flicker.
// see routine "newMapLabelPrintBufferFill" in the asm file.
// the nonstandard spacing conceals a rendering artifact:
// when switching between floors, the game redraws the
// labels without erasing the old ones to make it seem
// as though only the number changes.
// but since for us, 1 character != 2 tiles, a small
// "flicker" will appear as the redraw occurs (since text
// is sent to the nametable procedurally).
// spacing the text like this hides the flicker within
// the space between the "e" and "r" in "Tower".
// ...in Gens. in Fusion it's between the "w" and "e".
// and i expect it'll turn out that on real hardware, it
// wouldn't have been visible except that i made this change.
// whaaaatever! - s

#ENDSCRIPT()

#STARTSCRIPT(0x9E39C)

[maplabel]
// 魔導塔地下[buffer1char]階
//Magic Tower Basement Floor [buffer1char]

//Tower Floor B[buffer1char]
[space2px]Tower[space3px]Floor[space3px]B[buffer5char][space2px]
[end]
// same as above - s

#STARTSCRIPT(0x9FBEA)

// okay, so as best i can tell, the game was designed to work like this:
// 1. enemy gets defeated
// 2. enemy defeat animation + messages play, automatically, and
//    display for a fixed amount of time
// 3. enemy defeat message disappears
// 4. arle's "yaaay" plays
// the problem: the game really does nothing to ensure proper synchronization
// of all these messages. arle's "yaaay" could show up at almost any time,
// as it will be delayed until any animation arle is in has finished.
// also, some enemies incorrectly set the flag to trigger arle's "yaaay"
// too soon, causing their final defeat message to vanish almost immediately
// (if arle is not in the middle of an animation to delay it).
// and in the worst case, if the clear command gets executed while the
// enemy's defeat message is still being printed, the box will get cleared
// but the message will continue printing, causing the first part of the message
// to disappear.
// 
// all of this is to explain that i've commented out the clear command below
// to avoid these issues. the result is that enemy defeat messages consistently
// remain on screen throughout arle's "yaaay" message, where before they were
// inconsistent and sometimes caused very noticeable display errors.
// phew.

//[clearall]

[leftbox]
// わぁーーーい！！
Yaaay!
[delay]<$0028>
[wait]

[kill]

#ENDSCRIPT()

#STARTSCRIPT(0x9FC06)

[clear]
[voice50]<$000E>
[leftbox]
// ダメです。[br]
// ぼく、[br]
// ばたんきゅー。
Oh no...[br]
Lights out for me...
[sound]<$0014>
[kill]

#ENDSCRIPT()

[leftbox]
// ダッシュで[br]
// 逃げるっ！
I'm outta here!
[autoend]

#ENDSCRIPT()

You trip.

[autoend]

#ENDSCRIPT()

#STARTSCRIPT(0xA02D0)

[voice50]<$0081>
[rightbox2]
[clear]
// 「今だけ[br]
// こうげきりょくを[br]
// 貸してあげるわ」
{I shall lend you some strength.}

// NOTE: this delay has been changed to fix a bug
// which was probably introduced by the translation's slower
// text rendering.
// the original delay is just long enough that, if the enemy has
// an attack queued for after the lipemco message ends, the [clearall]
// will take effect immediately *after* that message starts printing.
// this results in the top part of the message getting blanked out
// while the rest prints normally.
// by shortening this delay and making up the difference after the
// clear occurs, we prevent this issue.
// (this may only apply to the defense up/down messages, but i've changed
// these too just in case)
//
// double NOTE: upon further examination, i'm fairly certain the
// problem actually lies with the attack/defense decreased code
// itself, which seems to "unlock" the enemy's actions too soon
// compared to the other LIPEMCO effects.
// well, i don't want to alter the timing of something gameplay-related,
// so this will have to do.
//[delay]<$0096>
[delay]<$0094>

[leftbox2]
// こうげきりょくが[br]
// パワーアップ！
Attack increased!
[op3C]
[clearall]

// NOTE: added due to bugfix described above
[delay]<$0002>

[end]

#ENDSCRIPT()

#STARTSCRIPT(0xA0330)

[voice50]<$0081>
[rightbox2]
[clear]
// 「今だけ[br]
// こうげきりょくを[br]
// 借りるわね」
{I shall borrow some strength.}

//[delay]<$0096>
[delay]<$0094>

[leftbox2]
// こうげきりょくが[br]
// パワーダウン。[br]
// とほほ・・・
Attack decreased. Awww...
[op3C]
[clearall]

// NOTE: added due to bugfix described above
[delay]<$0002>

[end]

#ENDSCRIPT()

#STARTSCRIPT(0xA0AB6)

// 酸素の素
Oxygen Gummy
[kill]
// ID = 0x23
// note: never actually obtained in-game. according to the narration,
// arle "gets" and "uses" it immediately, which really just means the
// game is setting the flag that allows you to enter the basement.
// hacking it into the inventory reveals that it has its own
// graphics and actually does function as an item, but using it
// just has the same effect as a golden apple. - s

#STARTSCRIPT(0xA0AE2)

// 魔導メモ
Sorcery Memo
[kill]
// ID = 0x27
// this isn't a used item.
// this term is used in the game's manual to refer to a
// section at the end of the manual where you're meant to
// write down the commands for the spells you learn,
// so perhaps this item was meant to show the spells you know
// in-game (like the battle help menu).
// hacked into the inventory, it has the same icon as the grimoires
// you learn spells from and acts as a health-restoring consumable. - s

#ENDSCRIPT()

#STARTSCRIPT(0xA1712)
//Puyoman
[leftbox]
// ぷよぷよに[br]
// にている[br]
// おまんじゅう。
//Steamed bun shaped like a Puyo.

// so, one of the game's problems is "insert something sweet
// into this hole", and the solution is to insert a Puyoman.
// but it's not obvious to a non-Japanese person that a
// "steamed bun" is something "sweet".
// also puyoman are possibly pounded rice cakes rather than
// just steamed buns.
// so here's something that's hopefully a little more intuitive.
Steamed cake shaped like a Puyo.
[wait]

[kill]

#ENDSCRIPT()

//===========================================================
// enemy battle messages
//===========================================================

// NOTE: the [wait] commands have been commented out of all enemy defeat
// messages due to a bug -- boxes ended with [wait] can be closed by pressing
// a button. these messages display automatically, so they don't need
// it in the first place. having it just meant that if the player mashed
// the button, they could make the message disappear before it was supposed to.

//=======================================
// enemy 0 battle messages
//=======================================

// NOTE: this clear command was not in the original game.
// this is a bug that went unnoticed -- the text is printed
// into the box without getting rid of the "まものだ！" text
// that is already there. this causes the next line to
// incorrectly, but plausibly, display as "え゛！？！"
// of course, it looks much worse in the translation, hence
// this extra command.
[clear]

// え゛！？
What the--?!

// NOTE: this delay command was not in the original game either!
// this time, it's added to fix a bug:
// if arle's text box here is cleared before lala's wall-busting
// animation progresses far enough, the game will freeze
// (probably due to spinning indefinitely waiting for
// one of the synchronization flags to equal some value that it's
// already passed, since several of them are changed immediately
// after the wait command).
// adding this delay prevents the box from being closed until
// it's safe to do so.
// for the record, a delay of 32 frames is _probably_ enough,
// but let's play it safe and go with 60.
[delay]<$003C>

[wait]

// we're doing something incompatible, so i've added
// text clears between boxes to keep things working. - s

[br]

[br]

//===========================================================
// intro and ending
//===========================================================

// note: unlike the normal dialogue window, these scenes have
// the text flush up against the left margin of the window.
// it looks fine with the japanese font, which has at least a
// pixel of space on the left side of every character, but
// the new font is all the way left-aligned to conserve space.
// thus, every line in these scenes begins with a 1-pixel space
// to prevent the text from abutting the window border.
// setting the break mode to OFFSET1PX causes this to also be
// applied to any automatic line breaks.
#SETBREAKMODE(OFFSET1PX)



#SETSIZE(256, 3)

#STARTSCRIPT(0xB1146)

[face]<$A29C>
[centerbox28]
// 『起きんかぁーーーっ！！』
//[space1px]<WAKE UP ALREADY!!>

[space1px]{WAKE UP ALREADY!!}
[autoend]
// note: these aren't displayed in the original game.
// the message matches up with the voice clip in the intro, though.
// perhaps they use this before the voice clip was implemented.
// since we want the player to know what the voice clip says, I've
// added the second version of this below back into the game
// over the "pokan" scene.

#ENDSCRIPT()

// this bears some explanation...
// for some reason, rather than writing a proper routine to
// clear the center dialogue box in these cutscenes,
// the developers chose to fake it by printing out this box of
// nothing but spaces every single time they wanted to clear
// the box.
// this works in the original game, but due to differences in how
// the hack prints text, it causes problems if replicated as-is.
// so i added an opcode to clear the center box.
// why they didn't have one in the first place, i don't know.
// maybe they were trying to avoid lagging the game by distributing
// the clear operation over multiple frames?
// well, it makes no difference as far as i can tell, so whatever.

#ENDSCRIPT()

#SETBREAKMODE(NORMAL)







//===========================================================
// monster names
//===========================================================

// in the original game, monster names, alone of all other
// text in the game, are stored in a fixed-length table
// rather than as scripts.
// they've been converted to scripts for our purposes.
// the original strings will get overwritten with jump commands
// that are copied to the dynamic print buffer.
// the buffer print routine will now check for
// jump commands in the buffer before running it, redirecting
// these to the new scripts (and removing the character limit).

//=======================================
// monster name 0
//=======================================

#STARTSCRIPT(0x9ED1C)

// みどりぷよ　
Green Puyo
[kill]

#ENDSCRIPT()

//=======================================
// monster name 1
//=======================================

//Green Puyo
